2:26:1475:0:14:72:483:700:12:Times:12:Times:Provider Incentives and Healthcare Costs:  Evidence from Long-Term Care Hospitals
2:27:1556:14:14:72:318:686:12:Times:12:Times:Liran Einav, Amy Finkelstein, and Neale Mahoney
2:28:1603:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:NBER Working Paper No. 23100
2:29:1631:14:14:72:136:658:12:Times:12:Times:January 2017
2:30:1643:14:28:72:177:644:12:Times:12:Times:JEL No. D22,I11,L21
2:31:1662:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:ABSTRACT
2:32:1670:28:14:72:546:588:12:Times:12:Times:We  study  the  design  of  provider  incentives  in  the  post-acute  care  setting –  a  high-stakes  but 
2:33:1778:14:14:72:545:574:12:Times:12:Times:under-studied segment of the healthcare system. We focus on long-term care hospitals (LTCHs) 
2:34:1870:14:14:72:546:560:12:Times:12:Times:and  the  large  (approximately$13,000)  jump  in  Medicare  payments  they  receive  when  a  patient's 
2:35:1975:14:14:72:545:546:12:Times:12:Times:stay  reaches  a  threshold  number of  days.  The  descriptive  evidence  indicates  that  discharges 
2:36:2077:14:14:72:545:532:12:Times:12:Times:increase  substantially  after  the  threshold, and  that  the  marginal  patient  discharged  after  the 
2:37:2182:14:14:72:546:518:12:Times:12:Times:threshold  is  in  relatively  better  health.  Despite  the large  financial  incentives  and  behavioral 
2:38:2288:14:14:72:545:504:12:Times:12:Times:response  in  a  high  mortality  population,  we  are  unable  to detect  any  compelling  evidence  of  an 
2:39:2396:14:14:72:546:490:12:Times:12:Times:impact on patient mortality. To assess provider behavior under counterfactual payment schedules, 
2:40:2492:14:14:72:546:476:12:Times:12:Times:we  estimate  a  simple  dynamic  discrete  choice  model  of  LTCH discharge  decisions.  When  we 
2:41:2591:14:14:72:546:462:12:Times:12:Times:conservatively limit ourselves to alternative contracts that hold the LTCH harmless, we find that 
2:42:2688:14:14:72:546:448:12:Times:12:Times:an alternative contract can generate Medicare savings of about $2,100 per admission, or about 5% 
2:43:2784:14:14:72:545:434:12:Times:12:Times:of  total  payments.  More  aggressive  payment  reforms  can  generate  substantially  greater savings, 
2:44:2888:14:14:72:546:420:12:Times:12:Times:but the accompanying reduction in LTCH profits has potential out-of-sample consequences. Our 
2:45:2980:14:14:72:545:406:12:Times:12:g_d0_f1:results  highlight  how  improved  financial  incentives  may  be  able  to  reduce  healthcare  spending, 
2:46:3086:14:28:72:399:392:12:Times:12:Times:without negative consequences for industry profits or patient health.
2:47:3155:28:14:72:129:364:12:Times:12:Times:Liran Einav
2:48:3166:14:14:72:167:350:12:Times:12:Times:Stanford University
2:49:3185:14:14:72:198:336:12:Times:12:Times:Department of Economics
2:50:3208:14:14:72:144:322:12:Times:12:Times:579 Serra Mall
2:51:3222:14:14:72:200:308:12:Times:12:Times:Stanford, CA  94305-6072
2:52:3246:14:14:72:124:294:12:Times:12:Times:and NBER
2:53:3254:14:28:72:172:280:12:Times:12:Times:leinav@stanford.edu
2:54:3273:28:14:72:152:252:12:Times:12:Times:Amy Finkelstein
2:55:3288:14:14:72:245:238:12:Times:12:Times:Department of Economics, E52-442
2:56:3320:14:14:72:94:224:12:Times:12:Times:MIT

2:66:3487:14:14:306:358:294:12:Times:12:Times:and NBER
